in touch\n\n]\\(/contact)\n\n[Login](https://app.klue.com/)\n\n[GET A DEMO](#)\n\nArticle\n\nThe Ultimate 7-Step Guide to Win-Loss Analysis (2025)\n\nBy [Adam McQueen](/blog/authors/adam-mcqueen) 19 min read\nDecember 3, 2025\n\nEvery quarter, leadership teams worldwide pore over CRM data and sales notes looking to glean insights about why they’re winning and losing sales deals. \n\nWhat they’re doing is searching for patterns. Patterns that could improve sales strategy, inform product decisions, and boost win rates. Yet the explanations they encounter always feel frustratingly familiar:\n\n“Our price was too high”\n\n“We were missing X features”\n\n“They went with competitor Y”\n\nHere’s the reality: understanding why you really win and lose deals requires more than CRM data and sales team hunches.\n\nYou need unfiltered feedback straight from your buyers and a system to capture and analyze that feedback. \n\nThe solution? Win-loss analysis. \n\nA gaining popularity\n\nIn this guide, we’ll share everything you need to know about building a win-loss program from the ground up.\n\nPlus, here’s a [win-loss analysis template](https://go.klue.com/win-loss-analysis-template) you can download and use alongside this guide.\n\n💡 Did you know? In 2025, 98% of win-loss programs have executive visibility. For more stats like this, check our [2025 Win-Loss Trends Report](http://%F0%9F%92%A1%20Did%20you%20know?%20In%202025,%2098%%20of%20win-loss%20programs%20now%20have%20executive%20visibility.%20We%20surveyed%20300+%20Check%20out%202025%20win-loss%20trends%20report%20for%20more%20stats%20like%20this.) (we surveyed 300+ leaders!).\n\nHow to establish Win-Loss Analysis\n\n[1. What Is Win-Loss Analysis?](#What_Is_Win-Loss_Analysis)\n\n[2. The Four Stages of Win-Loss Maturity](#The_Four_Stages_of_Win-Loss_Maturity)\n\n[3. Why You Need a Mature Win-Loss Program](#Why_You_Need_a_Mature_Win-Loss_Program)\n\n[4. How to Conduct a Win-Loss Analysis in 7 Steps](#How_to_Conduct_a_Win-Loss_Analysis_in_7_Steps)\n\n[5. Step 1. Rally Your Win-Loss Stakeholders (Get Program Buy-In)](#Step_1_Rally_Your_Win-Loss_Stakeholders_Get_Program_Buy-In)\n\n[6. Step 2. Get Clear On Your Win-Loss Learning Objectives & Strategy](#Step_2_Get_Clear_On_Your_Win-Loss_Learning_Objectives_Strategy)\n\n[7. Step 3: Calculate Your Win-Rates and Win-Loss Ratio](#Step_3_Calculate_Your_Win-Rates_and_Win-Loss_Ratio)\n\n[8. Step 4: Create Your Win-Loss Interviews (Human + AI-Led)](#Step_4_Create_Your_Win-Loss_Interviews_Human_AI-Led)\n\n[9. Test drive the Win-Loss AI Interviewer yourself here.](#Test_drive_the_Win-Loss_AI_Interviewer_yourself_here)\n\n[9.1. Step 5. Conduct Your Interviews](#Step_5_Conduct_Your_Interviews)\n\n[9.2. Step 6: Analyze Your Win-Loss Data](#Step_6_Analyze_Your_Win-Loss_Data)\n\n[9.3. Step 7: Present Your Findings](#Step_7_Present_Your_Findings)\n\n[9.4. Time to Get the Full Picture](#Time_to_Get_the_Full_Picture)\n\nWhat Is Win-Loss Analysis?\n\nWin-loss analysis is a process that leverages buyer interviews and surveys to help companies understand the reasons behind their successes (wins) and failures (losses) in sales deals.\n\nBy looking at both won and lost opportunities – and hearing directly from buyers about the reasons behind these outcomes – win-loss analysis gives you unbiased insights into:\n\nYour product – where it shines and where it falls short.\n\nYour sales experience – how buyers feel about interactions with your team.\n\nYour marketing – whether your messaging and campaigns resonate.\n\nYour buyer’s priorities – what matters most to your customers.\n\nYour competitive position – how you compare to your competitors. \n\nWith these insights, you can work to improve your product, refine your messaging, coach your sales team, improve your [compete program](https://klue.com/blog/bring-win-loss-into-compete-content) and ultimately improve your overall win rate.\n\nThe Four Stages of Win-Loss Maturity\n\nIt’s not uncommon for companies to think they’re doing win-loss analysis. \n\nBut there’s a big difference between tracking basic deal outcomes in a CRM and running a cross-functional program that actually drives change.\n\nTo help companies assess their win-loss efforts and chart a path forward, [Ryan Sorely](https://www.linkedin.com/in/ryansorley/), founder of Klue Win-Loss, developed the “Four Stages of Win-Loss Progam Maturity.” \n\nIf you’re just getting started, this framework will help you understand where your program stands today and what it takes to reach the next level. \n\na graph representing the 4 stages of win-loss program maturity\n\nLet’s look at each stage:\n\nStage 1: Sales-Sourced: Your sales team gathers some buyer feedback, typically via dropdown codes in your CRM. But there’s no formal process, just sporadic insights based on what sales reps remember or choose to share. This leads to incomplete and often biased data.\n\nStage 2: Siloed: One department runs win-loss analysis, but insights aren’t shared widely across your organization, limiting the potential impact on overall business strategy.\n\nStage 3: Integrated: You have a dedicated program owner collecting data across all buyer touchpoints. However leadership buy-in may be lacking, and there’s no structured approach to turn those insights into action.\n\nStage 4: Action-Oriented: A dedicated owner oversees the program, and there’s strong cross-functional alignment and leadership support. Insights are reviewed regularly by key stakeholders, data is collected systematically, and most importantly, specific, measurable actions are taken based on these insights.\n\nWhy You Need a Mature Win-Loss Program\n\n\n\nIf your program is in Stage 1 or 2 of Ryan’s Win-Loss Program Maturity Model (see previous section), you’re probably thinking: “We’re already collecting feedback and using it to make decisions. Isn’t that enough?”\n\nHere’s why those early stages aren’t enough:\n\n1\\. Your Sales Team Shouldn’t Run Win-Loss\n\nAccording to [Anova Consulting](https://theanovagroup.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/Win_Loss_Analysis_Book_Chapter_1.pdf), 60% of sellers are partially or completely wrong about why they lost a deal. And it’s not their fault – a seller’s job is to sell, not conduct win-loss analysis. Every minute they spend on analysis is a minute not spent chasing leads and closing deals. Most reps will (and should) focus on the latter.\n\n2\\. Your CRM Data Is Probably Misleading\n\nBad CRM data could be skewing your win-loss analysis. Just look at the numbers:\n\n91% of CRM data is incomplete ([Salesforce](https://www.salesforce.com/ca/resources/research-reports/state-of-crm/))\n\n70% becomes inaccurate annually ([Salesforce](https://www.salesforce.com/ca/resources/research-reports/state-of-crm/))\n\nMost win-loss data gets recorded through dropdown codes that sellers rush to fill out with vague options like “budget”, “no decision”, or “bad timing.” The result? Strategic decisions get based on outdated, half-baked information.\n\nWant to learn more? Check out our [deep dive](https://klue.com/blog/why-youre-in-the-dark-about-your-deals-and-how-to-fix-it) on why CRM data might be leaving you in the dark when it comes to understanding deal dynamics.\n\n3\\. Buyers Won’t Tell Sales The Truth\n\nThink about it: when was the last time you told a salesperson the real reason you didn’t buy? Buyers often:\n\nGive vague answers to avoid awkward conversations\n\nHide their true decision criteria\n\nSugarcoat negative feedback\n\nPro Tip: If you want fast-track your program from “Sales-Sourced” to “Action-Oriented,” [Klue Win-Loss](https://klue.com/win-loss) can help:\n\nCentralize all buyer insights\n\nAutomate data collection\n\nSpot patterns with AI\n\nShare findings instantly\n\nThe result? Skip months of manual work and build a mature program faster.\n\nHow to Conduct a Win-Loss Analysis in 7 Steps\n\nNow that we’re clear on the fundamentals, let’s get tactical. Here are the seven steps you need to take to stand up a win-loss program at your org.\n\nStep 1. Rally Your Win-Loss Stakeholders (Get Program Buy-In)\n\na graphic for a stakeholder survey that can be used for a win-loss program\n\nA win-loss program thrives on organizational support. That means before you start collecting data, you’ll need to secure buy-in with the right people. \n\nTo do this, map out what departments at your organization interact with your customers and then mao out what insights those stakeholders likely need most. Chances are:\n\nProduct is dying to know what features make or break deals\n\nMarketing is eager for messaging validation data\n\nSales leaders are interested in process and execution gaps\n\nExecutives want deep buyer insights to guide big-picture decisions\n\nYour job? Make sure your program addresses these needs from day one. When stakeholders see their priorities reflected in your strategy, they become advocates instead of obstacles.\n\nLet’s discuss how to go about securing buy-in with a few key stakeholders…\n\nCEO/C-Suite\n\nGetting C-suite buy-in is critical – it secures not just approval, but the resources needed to run an effective program. The good news? These conversations are often simpler than you might expect.\n\nMost executives lack clear visibility into why deals succeed or fail. Their understanding typically comes from filtered CRM data and second-hand sales reports. This creates a perfect opening for win-loss analysis.\n\nHere’s how a typical conversation might flow:\n\n“Do you feel you truly know why we’re winning and losing deals?”\n\nWhen they acknowledge the gap – and they usually do – explain how [win-loss interviews](https://klue.com/blog/win-loss-interviews) can provide:\n\nDirect buyer feedback on deal outcomes\n\nInsights into selection criteria and business drivers\n\nClear data on product, pricing, and sales effectiveness\n\nMonthly analysis of findings and recommendations\n\nFrame the program as an enhancement to existing processes rather than a major new initiative. When executives see the potential impact relative to the minimal time investment required, approval often comes naturally.\n\nWatch: Hunter breaks down how he presents win-loss insights to Klue’s exec team 👇\n\nFunctional Leaders\n\nDepartment leaders need clear evidence that win-loss insights will drive tangible results. The key is involving them in program design from day one through a focused stakeholder survey:\n\nWhat insights would most impact your team’s goals?\n\nWhich three questions would you ask buyers directly?\n\nHow will you use these findings to drive specific actions?\n\nThis targeted approach serves multiple purposes:\n\nCreates early buy-in through active collaboration\n\nReveals each leader’s unique priorities and blind spots\n\nEstablishes clear plans for implementing insights\n\nProvides accountability for using the data\n\nFor example, your Head of Sales might focus on team performance metrics, while your Head of Product needs data about feature gaps and engineering priorities. By documenting these needs upfront, you create both a roadmap for your program and a reference point for future alignment.\n\nSales Team\n\nYour sales team can either be your biggest champion or your main roadblock. Most hear “win-loss” and think “deal inspection.” Here’s how to flip that perception:\n\nMake it clear this is about improving the whole go-to-market motion\n\nShow how win-loss insights help close more deals\n\nTurn win-loss data into [competitive insights](https://klue.com/blog/competitive-insight) they can leverage\n\nKeep their involvement light (just warm buyer introductions)\n\nThe key? Show them it’s not just about sales. The less it feels like a performance review, the more they’ll champion your program.\n\nStep 2. Get Clear On Your Win-Loss Learning Objectives & Strategy\n\na graphic showing how to identify win-loss program learning objectives\n\nYour program needs a focused strategy right from the get-go. To help with this, we recommend defining clear learning objectives for your program and doing so with your stakeholders. \n\nLearning objectives are the specific insights you want to uncover with your program.\n\nThey should:\n\nAlign with company goals\n\nAddress stakeholder needs\n\nDrive specific actions\n\nBe measurable\n\nFor example, let’s say your leadership team is considering a major pricing change.\n\nYour learning objective could be: “understand how pricing impacts buyer decisions across segments”\n\nHere, you’ll want to focus on uncovering:\n\nHow buyers perceive your pricing vs competitors\n\nWhich pricing discussions create friction in deals\n\nWhat objections sales struggles to overcome\n\nThe key is making your objectives specific and actionable.\n\nStep 3: Calculate Your Win-Rates and Win-Loss Ratio\n\nWhile win-loss analysis drives many benefits across your organization, there’s one clear measurable outcome: increasing your win rate.\n\nBut to show improvement, you need a baseline. Here are the two metrics that matter most, in our opinion, and how to calculate them. \n\nCalculating Your Win Rate\n\nYou can think of this as the fundamental performance metric for your win-loss program. A win rate is a sales metric that measures the percentage of deals closed (won) out of the total number of deals engaged.\n\nFor example: If you closed 100 deals last quarter and won 40 of them, your win rate is 40%.\n\nHere’s how you calculate it:\n\nWin Rate = (Number of Won Deals ÷ Total Number of Closed Deals) × 100\n\nCalculating Your Win-Loss Ratio\n\nYour win-loss ratio gives you a clearer picture of your overall competitive performance. It’s a metric that compares the number of deals won to the number of deals lost, expressed as a ratio.\n\nFor example: If you won 40 deals and lost 60, your win-loss ratio is 2:3.\n\nHere’s how you calculate it:\n\nWin-Loss Ratio = Number of Won Deals : Number of Lost Deals\n\nWhy these metrics matter:\n\nThey provide a clear baseline to measure program success\n\nThey help you set realistic improvement goals\n\nThey make it easy to demonstrate program ROI to stakeholders\n\nStep 4: Create Your Win-Loss Interviews (Human + AI-Led)\n\nA common question teams ask: “How do we balance depth and scale in win-loss?”\n\nFor years, the answer was “surveys for scale, interviews for depth.”\n\nBut surveys don’t capture much insight — and teams need more than checkboxes to understand why deals were won or lost.\n\nToday, the modern win-loss stack pairs AI-led interviews with human-led interviews:\n\nAI-led interviews give you scalable, structured insight across every deal.\n\nHuman-led interviews deliver deep, story-rich context on your most strategic accounts.\n\nTogether, they give you complete coverage: consistent signal across your pipeline and deep dives where it matters most.\n\nLet’s break down how to use each.\n\nAI-Led Win-Loss Interviews\n\nAI-led interviews act like a “lightweight interviewer” that reps or buyers can talk to for 2–5 minutes. They give you far more signal than a survey, without the time, logistics, or cost of running full interviews for every deal.\n\nThey’re perfect for:\n\nearly-stage and mid-market segments\n\npipeline-wide trend detection\n\nconsistent deal debriefs across your entire seller base\n\nunderstanding competitor presence, objections, friction, and positioning gaps\n\nHere’s how to get the most value from AI-led interviews:\n\n1\\. Tie Each Interview to a Learning Objective\n\nJust like human interviews, AI-led ones should probe toward a specific goal — why the deal moved, what buyers cared about, where messaging landed or didn’t.\n\nModern interviewers (like Klue’s) actually understand this objective and dynamically probe to hit it.\n\n2\\. Keep the Experience Fast and Natural\n\nThe key advantage of AI-led interviews is the simplicity — no scheduling, no chasing, no Zoom.\n\nReps or buyers talk in their own words, and you receive structured, tagged insights minutes later.\n\n3\\. Automate the Trigger\n\nLet your CRM fire interviews automatically when deals close, when a stage is hit, or when competitive pressure spikes. This ensures consistent coverage — something manual processes never achieve.\n\n4\\. Use AI for Theme-Spotting and Pattern Analysis\n\nThis is where AI-led interviews become far more powerful than surveys.\n\nInstead of raw transcripts, Klue automatically:\n\nsummarizes responses\n\ntags competitors, objections, friction, value drivers\n\ngroups signals across interviews into themes\n\nlinks every theme to the original quotes\n\nThis gives PMMs, Sales Leadership, and RevOps a clean, trustworthy signal without hours of manual analysis.\n\n[Test drive the Win-Loss AI Interviewer yourself here.](https://interviewer.klue.com/LdwYJWH)\n\nWin-Loss Interviews\n\nThese are one-on-one conversations with your buyers that provide rich, unfiltered insights into their decision-making process. While more time-intensive, they give you the deepest understanding of your wins and losses.\n\nHuman-led interviews are best used for:\n\nhigh-value or strategic accounts\n\nnuanced buying committees\n\ncompetitive displacement deals\n\npricing, packaging, and product-feedback deep dives\n\nHere’s how to run them effectively:\n\n1\\. Tie Questions to Objectives: Every question should connect back to your learning objectives from Step 2. If a question doesn’t help achieve your goals, skip it.\n\n2\\. Prepare More Questions Than You Need: Write 20-30 questions, expect to use 10-15. This gives you flexibility to explore valuable threads and ensures you’re prepared for any direction.\n\n3\\. Time It Right: Schedule 30-minute calls but block an hour for your calendar. Let good conversations run longer.\n\n4\\. Follow The Energy: When you hit on something insightful, don’t be afraid to go off-script with follow-up questions. Often the best insights come from these deeper explorations.\n\n5\\. Keep Questions Clear: Focus on one concept per question. Avoid complex, multi-part queries that lead to surface-level answers.\n\n6\\. Skip What You Know: Don’t waste time asking about the information you already have from your CRM or deal records. Focus on getting new insights.\n\nPro Tip: If you’ve already been recording your own win-loss interviews, make sure you’re getting the most out of them. Tools like Klue’s [Bring Your Own Interviews (BYOI)](https://klue.com/win-loss) feature let you upload your recordings directly into the platform. From there, the software automatically transcribes, analyzes, and tags key themes, making it easier than ever to extract actionable insights from your interviews. \n\nTo see a full demo of Klue’s BYOI feature, watch the video below👇\n\nThe Interview Guide\n\nBefore you dive straight into interviews, we recommend creating a thorough interview guide. \n\nYou can think of this as your blueprint for buyer conversations. It’s not a rigid script, but rather a structured framework that ensures you’re gathering insights that map back to your program learning objectives.\n\nInstead of compiling a random list of questions, focus on mapping key topics to your learning goals.\n\nTopics/learning objectives could include:\n\nBusiness Drivers: What triggered their search? Which problems needed solving?\n\nSelection Process: How did they go about finding a solution? What was their evaluation process?\n\nProduct Experience: What features mattered most? How well did the product meet their needs?\n\nPricing and Packaging: How do they view the pricing structure?What’s their take on overall value?\n\nSales Experience: How helpful was the sales team? What could have made the process better?\n\nBuying Process: Who made the final decision? What approvals were needed?\n\nDemo Experience: How effective was the demo? What stood out (good or bad)?\n\nBy the end of this process, you should have a document organized by key topics (all tied to your learning objectives) with 2-5 action-oriented questions under each.\n\nIf you’re stuck on what specific questions to ask, we’ve put together a list of 31 [best win-loss interview questions](https://klue.com/blog/31-best-win-loss-questions) for you to check out.\n\nStep 5. Conduct Your Interviews\n\nNow that you’re all set-up, it’s time to actually conduct your [win-loss interviews](https://klue.com/blog/win-loss-interviews).\n\nMost teams start by asking: “How many interviews should we do?”\n\nHere’s the truth – what matters isn’t quantity, but running focused interviews with the right people.\n\nLet’s break down how to do this right:\n\nRecruit the Right Win-Loss Interview Candidates\n\nGetting awe-inspiring insights starts with interviewing the right people. Here’s how to be strategic about your candidate selection:\n\nAlign With Learning Objectives: Use your program objectives to qualify candidates in or out.\n\nCreate Research Cohorts: Group your candidates by shared characteristics (product line, deal size, region). You need at least 10 similar deals to identify reliable patterns.\n\nTarget Late-Stage Deals: Focus on buyers who went deep into your sales process. They’ve seen everything – from demos to pricing – and can provide comprehensive feedback.\n\nFocus on Competitive Deals: Prioritize opportunities where you went head-to-head with specific competitors you want to learn more about.\n\nGo Through Sales: Have your sales team make the intro. They know the right contacts and their warm relationship leads to higher acceptance rates.\n\nTime Your Outreach Right: Contact buyers within 90 days of their decision. Any longer and memories fade; any sooner and you might disrupt active deals.\n\nGetting the Most Out of Your Interviews\n\nNo matter how well you’ve prepared up to this point, the interviews themselves will be the single biggest factor in determining the success or failure of your win-loss program.\n\nIf you want to dive deep into this topic, we interviewed Ryan Sorely (CEO of Klue Win-Loss) about how to [nail your first win-loss interview](https://klue.com/blog/how-to-nail-win-loss-interviews).\n\nIn the meantime, here are some key tips to get you started:\n\nMake It Clear That This Isn’t a Sales Call: Start by letting them know you’re not trying to revive the deal. You’re here to learn.\n\nPick Your Interviewer Wisely: Get someone who’s impartial, matches your buyer’s seniority level, and keeps their cool under pressure.\n\nTrain Those Interviewers: Show them the ropes – from deal research and warm-up chats to keeping the conversation flowing.\n\nCameras On: You’ll get better insights when you can see each other’s faces.\n\nMaster the “Five Whys”: When a buyer shares something important, start asking “why?” Take their answer and ask “why?” again. Keep going until you hit the root cause (usually 4-5 times deep).\n\na graphic showing how to use the 5 whys approach during a win-loss interview\n\nStep 6: Analyze Your Win-Loss Data\n\nYou’ve done the interviews. You’ve gathered the feedback. Now comes the make-or-break moment of your win-loss program – turning raw win-loss data into usable insights.\n\nThis is where many programs stumble. Teams either get overwhelmed by the mountain of data they’ve collected or rush to share disconnected findings that don’t tell a clear story.\n\nHere’s how to analyze your data effectively:\n\n1\\. Align Data With Your Program’s Learning Objectives\n\nGo through your transcripts and sort feedback based on your original learning objectives.\n\nFor example, if your objective was “Understand why enterprise deals choose competitors,” collect all feedback about:\n\nEnterprise requirements\n\nCompetitor selections\n\nDecision criteria\n\nDeal breakers\n\nSelection process\n\nThe beauty of a well-structured interview guide? Most answers will already align with your learning objectives and be neatly sorted on key topics. \n\n2\\. Text Tagging\n\nEven after aligning with objectives, you’ll have lots of unstructured data. Here’s how to organize it for easier analysis. \n\nIdentify key quotes from your transcripts\n\nAssign each quote a main topic and sub-topic\n\nExample: “Their product was easier to use than other vendors'”\n\nMain tag: Product \n\nSub tag: Ease of Use\n\nFor a complete guide on interview tagging, check out our blog post: [how to tag win-loss data](https://klue.com/blog/how-to-tag-win-loss-data).\n\n3\\. Automate Your Win-Loss Data Analysis\n\nIf manually tagging feels overwhelming, tools like Klue’s [360° Win-Loss](https://klue.com/win-loss) can do the heavy lifting. Its AI-powered tagging automatically organizes interview data into actionable themes, helping you uncover patterns like win-loss reasons, competitive gaps, and sales performance trends​.\n\nStep 7: Present Your Findings\n\nYou’ve done the hard work of collecting and analyzing your win-loss data. Now you get to share these insights across your organization.\n\nHere are the key ways we recommend presenting your findings:\n\nWin-Loss Deal Reports \n\nAfter each win-loss interview, create a detailed report about the specific deal discussed. \n\nThese reports help teams understand exactly what happened in specific deals. They should include:\n\nA clear “Why We Won/Lost” summary upfront\n\nKey findings tied to learning objectives\n\nDirect quotes from the buyer\n\nAnalysis of every deal stage (discovery through decision)\n\nPro tip: Always attach the interview recording and transcript to deal reports. Some stakeholders will want to dig deeper.\n\nWin-Loss Executive Summaries \n\nLet’s face it – executives love their summaries. And for good reason. These presentations help leadership spot patterns across deals and make strategic decisions.\n\nWith a win-loss executive summary, you’ll want focus on delivering the most value possible for senior leadership team. So, make sure your presentation emphasizes:\n\nThe biggest, most urgent insights that need attention\n\nClear trends emerging across multiple interviews\n\nData tied directly to your program’s most important learning objectives\n\nThese presentations are perfect for quarterly business reviews and board meetings where you need to tell a clear story about what’s happening in your deals.\n\nWin-Loss Sales Presentations \n\nYour sales team needs actionable [competitive intelligence](https://klue.com/blog/competitive-intelligence) that they can use in the field. These presentations will be goldmines for this. They also double as perfect for sales kickoffs and coaching sessions.\n\nStart with the wins – show your team what’s working:\n\nMost effective sales tactics\n\nSuccessful deal strategies to replicate\n\nPositive buyer feedback on team performance\n\nWinning competitive positioning\n\nThen tackle the challenges:\n\nCommon objections and how to handle them\n\nWhere deals get stuck in the process\n\nCompetitor mentions\n\nPro Tip: take your top insights and build them into your [sales battlecards](https://klue.com/blog/competitive-battlecards-101). Turn common objections into proven responses, competitor mentions into comparison points, and buyer pain points into targeted talk tracks. In our experience, win-loss insights offer some of the best [primary competitive intel](https://klue.com/blog/gathering-competitive-intelligence) available.\n\nIn this highly tactical Compete Week keynote, Hunter breaks down the five different ways he distributes win-loss intelligence at Klue👇\n\nTime to Get the Full Picture\n\nBuilding a win-loss program takes work. But now you have everything you need to start gathering the insights that will transform your business:\n\nA framework to assess your program\n\nSteps to get stakeholder buy-in\n\nTools to gather deep buyer feedback\n\nWays to turn insights into action\n\nRemember – getting a complete view of your wins and losses isn’t about any single data point. It’s about seeing the full 360-degree picture of why buyers choose you (or don’t).\n\nGood luck!\n\nSHARE THIS POST\n\n[](https://www.linkedin.com/sharing/share-offsite/?url=https://klue.com/blog/win-loss-analysis-guide)[](https://www.facebook.com/sharer/sharer.php?u=https://klue.com/blog/win-loss-analysis-guide)[](https://twitter.com/intent/tweet?text=Hello%20world\\&url=https://klue.com/blog/win-loss-analysis-guide)\n\nEXPERT GUIDE\n\nThe Ultimate Guide to Win-Loss Interviews\n\nGet 50+ interview questions for your next win-loss call.\n\n[DOWNLOAD NOW](https://go.klue.com/guide-for-conducting-competitive-win-loss-interviews)\n\nBrowse by category\n\n[AI](https://klue.com/blog/category/ai)\n\n[Battlecards](https://klue.com/blog/category/battlecards)\n\n[Competitive Enablement](https://klue.com/blog/category/competitive-enablement)\n\n[Win Loss](https://klue.com/blog/category/win-loss)\n\n[Sales](https://klue.com/blog/category/sales)\n\n[Product Marketing](https://klue.com/blog/category/product-marketing)\n\n[Klue](https://klue.com/blog/category/product-updates)\n\nBrowse by type\n\n[ARTICLES](https://klue.com/content-type/article)\n\n[COURSES](https://klue.com/content-type/course)\n\n[Product](https://klue.com/content-type/product)\n\n[Guides](https://klue.com/content-type/guide)\n\n[reports](https://klue.com/content-type/report)\n\n[templates](https://klue.com/content-type/template)\n\nWant to see Klue in action?\n\nLet’s do it. Here are the two metrics that matter most, in our opinion, and how to calculate them.\n\n### Calculating Your Win Rate\n\nYou can think of this as the fundamental performance metric for your win-loss program. A win rate is a sales metric that measures the percentage of deals closed (won) out of the total number of deals engaged.\n\nFor example: If you closed 100 deals last quarter and won 40 of them, your win rate is 40%.\n\nHere’s how you calculate it: [...] Here’s how you calculate it:\n\nWin Rate = (Number of Won Deals ÷ Total Number of Closed Deals) × 100\n\n### Calculating Your Win-Loss Ratio\n\nYour win-loss ratio gives you a clearer picture of your overall competitive performance. It’s a metric that compares the number of deals won to the number of deals lost, expressed as a ratio.\n\nFor example: If you won 40 deals and lost 60, your win-loss ratio is 2:3.\n\nHere’s how you calculate it:\n\nWin-Loss Ratio = Number of Won Deals : Number of Lost Deals\n\n### Why these metrics matter:\n\n They provide a clear baseline to measure program success\n They help you set realistic improvement goals\n They make it easy to demonstrate program ROI to stakeholders\n\n## Step 4: Create Your Win-Loss Interviews (Human + AI-Led) [...] With these insights, you can work to improve your product, refine your messaging, coach your sales team, improve your compete program and ultimately improve your overall win rate.\n\n## The Four Stages of Win-Loss Maturity\n\nIt’s not uncommon for companies to think they’re doing win-loss analysis.\n\nBut there’s a big difference between tracking basic deal outcomes in a CRM and running a cross-functional program that actually drives change.\n\nTo help companies assess their win-loss efforts and chart a path forward, Ryan Sorely, founder of Klue Win-Loss, developed the “Four Stages of Win-Loss Progam Maturity.”\n\nIf you’re just getting started, this framework will help you understand where your program stands today and what it takes to reach the next level.\n\nLet’s look at each stage:\n\nTitle: The true ROI of win-loss analysis - Diffly\nURL: https://www.diffly.co/blog/the-true-roi-of-win-loss-analysis\nContent: Win-loss analysis doesn’t just analyze your performance; it monetizes it. The B2B Sales Methodology That Changes How Buyers Think | by Ewan Mak | Jan, 2026 | Medium\nURL: https://medium.com/%40tentenco/what-is-insight-selling-the-b2b-sales-methodology-that-changes-how-buyers-think-db970452ffe2\nPublished: 2026-01-28T00:00:00.000Z\nAuthor: Ewan Mak\nHighlights:\nB2B Sales Methodology That Changes How Buyers Think\n\nEwan Mak\n\n8 min read  ...    The traditional playbook for B2B sales no longer works. According to Gartner’s 2024 survey of 632 B2B buyers, 61% prefer a rep-free buying experience, and 73% actively avoid vendors who send irrelevant outreach. By the time buyers contact sales, they’ve already completed 57% to 80% of their purchase journey independently. This shift has rendered the classic “diagnose and prescribe” sales model obsolete. Insight Selling emerged as a direct  ...    An Insight Selling rep would lead with data: “Our research shows that proposals with embedded video and interactive pricing close 25% faster and receive 30% fewer scope change requests. Most companies think the delay happens during the  ...    Three structural changes in the B2B buying environment have made Insight Selling essential. First, information has been democratized. Buyers can easily research product specifications, competitive comparisons, and user reviews online. According to McKinsey, B2B buyers now consult an average of 10 digital sources before making a purchase decision. When product information is no longer scarce, salespeople who can only deliver what buyers already  ...    Second, buying committees have grown more complex. Gartner research indicates that B2B purchase decisions involve 5 to 16 stakeholders on average, spanning up to 4 departments. Each decision-maker brings independently gathered information to the table, making consensus harder to achieve. In fact, 74% of B2B buyer teams experience  ...    Third, price competition has intensified. When buyers complete most of their research before engaging sales, they enter  ... Seven use cases show how B2B leaders can maximize benefits and drive sustainable impact with a tailored gen AI strategy.  ...    **B2B leaders**are accustomed to using technology to help them achieve profitable growth. Lately they’ve been looking at a technology that hasthe potential to accelerate sales transformationsacross the entire seller journey—gen AI. Gen AI can helpdrive outsized, profitable growthby boosting revenue generation, increasing sales productivity, and streamlining internal processes. These leaders believe the potential is great. According toMcKinsey’s latest B2B Pulse Surveyof B2B decision-makers, 19 percent of respondents are already implementing gen AI use cases for B2B buying and selling, and another 23 percent are in the process of doing so. That’s promising. However, the flip side is that most B2B leaders have yet to embrace gen AI or even engage with it. A few leaders tell us they are unsure where the benefits would come from and whether the business impact justifies the investment. Some feel overwhelmed by the abundance of ideas and seek advice on what to prioritize. In this article, we explore seven compelling use cases across the deal cycle by analyzing gen AI deployments and their impact on sales ROI and customer experience (exhibit).1Gen AI is most often deployed in combination with analytical AI and machine learning (as well as other broader AI capabilities), often strengthening them. In this article, we use “AI” to refer to the full set of AI capabilities including gen AI. We use “gen AI” when referring only to*that*specific subset of AI.These use cases can improve effectiveness and efficiency and start delivering near-immediate impact. We also examine actual deployments by leading organizations. Finally, we suggest key considerations that can help organizations establish a gen AI implementation strategy that aligns with their goals and desires to drive  ... Bain & Company, for example, recommends that B2B companies should aim for a 60% response rate to their NPS surveys. In comparison, consumer-focused brands will typically struggle to ever reach 50%.\n\nThat means more meaningful feedback. NPS is seriously limited if you’re simply asking questions and failing to respond. But in B2B NPS, it’s much easier to close the loop and deliver value for both you and your customers. Although it works a little differently, it should be even more valuable than in B2C contexts.\n\nWhy? Because when each customer is worth so much more, saving large accounts from churning is possibly mission critical.\n\nNPS is the most effective way to do just that. All of the NPS benefits that you would expect from B2C are just as relevant in B2B too:\n\nIt’s simple, scalable, and delivers immediate insight. Conventional customer satisfaction surveys can be long-winded, convoluted, and can suffer from a low response rate. NPS performs so well—for B2B and B2C—because it’s straightforward and fast for both you and your customers.\n\nTitle: Measuring NPS for B2B - Cliezen\nURL: https://www.cliezen.com/blog/measuring-nps-for-b2b\nContent: NPS is a particularly important metric for B2B companies because of its strong correlation with customer loyalty, retention, and ultimately, revenue. This allows them to take actionable steps to improve overall satisfaction, whether by addressing specific issues raised by detractors or by learning from the positive experiences of promoters. [...] ### How is NPS used for B2B companies?\n\nIn the context of B2B companies, NPS serves as a valuable tool to measure customer loyalty and satisfaction. It can help identify areas in the customer journey that may need improvement, thus providing a roadmap for enhancing the customer experience. Additionally, NPS can be used as a benchmarking tool, allowing B2B companies to compare their performance against competitors and evaluate the effectiveness of their marketing and sales initiatives. It's a versatile metric that can provide actionable insights to drive business growth.\n\n### Why is NPS an important metric to measure for B2B companies? [...] ### What is NPS?\n\nNet Promoter Score, or NPS, is a powerful customer feedback metric that was developed by Bain & Company. It's designed to measure the likelihood of customers recommending your product or service to others. The simplicity of NPS lies in its single-question format, which asks, “On a scale of 0-10, how likely are you to recommend our product or service to a friend or colleague?” The responses to this question can provide a wealth of insight into customer satisfaction and loyalty.\n\n### How is NPS used for B2B companies?\n\nTitle: Loyalty and NPS at B2B Companies - Net Promoter System\nURL: https://www.netpromotersystem.com/about/building-loyalty-at-b2b-companies/\nContent: #### About NPS\n\n##### Important Concepts\n\n#### Resources\n\n##### Interactive tool\n\n#### Contact\n\n#### About NPS\n\n##### Important Concepts\n\n#### Resources\n\n##### Interactive tool\n\n#### Contact Us\n\n###### Popular Searches\n\n###### Your Previous Searches\n\n###### Recently Visited Pages\n\nContent added to Red Folder\n\nRemoved from Red Folder\n\nAbout\n\n# Building Loyalty at B2B Companies\n\n# Building Loyalty at B2B Companies\n\nNPS® correlates closely with greater market share, better employee engagement and higher profitability in B2B companies. Companies generally measure these scores through a double-blind process in which the respondent doesn’t know who is sponsoring the survey and the company can’t trace back responses to any individual respondent. Bottom-up surveys, on the other hand, are openly sponsored by the company, and the company keeps track of who responds. They often take place after particular transactions. Enterprise, for instance, surveys a sample of its customers within a few days of the end of their rentals. In B2B relationships or some [...] Precise, granular scores\n\nCompanies don’t measure profit only at the corporate level; they break it down by business, product line, geographic region, plant, store and so on. Granular performance measurements enable individuals and small teams to make better decisions and to be held responsible for the results. Strong Net Promoter metrics require the same kind of precision and granularity. At Enterprise, for instance, the crucial breakthrough was pushing the measurement of customer loyalty down to the level of individual branches. The specificity of the data both allowed and encouraged employees to be much more responsive to customer feedback. [...] Identifying the right customers is also important in B2B situations, but it can be even more challenging. Consider the situation of Philips Healthcare, which sells radiology equipment and services to hospitals and clinics. Relevant customer contacts include hospital CEOs and CFOs, heads of radiology, respected physicians, nurses and the technicians who operate the machines. At first, Philips’s Net Promoter researchers didn’t do enough up-front work to identify the right decision makers, influencers and users to survey. The numbers they reported to corporate each month were based on small samples from mixes of customers, resulting in volatile scores. Rather than pulling back from NPS, however, the Philips leadership team stepped up the effort to design a reliable measurement system, and by"}]}]},"uuid":"89582b14-d3c9-4f06-8b33-5a7e0ffdbca3","timestamp":"2026-03-22T05:07:10.270Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"a450f3de-6ba9-4ca4-b913-7b38017dc593","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-desktop","cwd":"/Users/mikerodgers/Startup-Intelligence-OS","sessionId":"6fa4d940-41fb-4efd-bc6a-1002703965b6","version":"2.1.78","gitBranch":"main","slug":"eventual-tinkering-map"}

Let me compile the complete research findings.\n\n---\n\n# Win/Loss Analysis: Deep Research Report\n## Methodologies from Top Consulting Firms & Specialized Platforms\n\nAll findings sourced from web searches and scrapes conducted March 2026. No training data used.\n\n---\n\n## 1. KLUE — The Competitive Enablement + Win-Loss Leader\n\n**Source URLs:**\n- https://klue.com/blog/win-loss-analysis-guide\n- https://klue.com/blog/win-loss-analysis-statistics\n- https://klue.com/blog/31-best-win-loss-questions\n- https://klue.com/win-loss\n\n### Methodology: 7-Step Win-Loss Framework\n\n1. **Rally Stakeholders** — Map departments that interact with customers, identify what insights each needs. Get CEO/C-suite, functional leaders, and sales team buy-in before collecting data.\n2. **Define Learning Objectives & Strategy** — Set specific, measurable learning objectives aligned with company goals (e.g., \"understand how pricing impacts buyer decisions across segments\").\n3. **Calculate Baseline Win Rates** — Win Rate = (Won Deals / Total Closed Deals) x 100. Win-Loss Ratio = Won : Lost.\n4. **Create Interviews (Human + AI-Led)** — Modern stack pairs AI-led interviews (scalable, 2-5 min, automated from CRM triggers) with human-led interviews (30-60 min, for strategic accounts).\n5. **Conduct Interviews** — Target late-stage deals, focus on competitive deals, contact within 90 days, warm intro from sales rep.\n6. **Analyze Data** — Align with learning objectives, text-tag quotes by topic/sub-topic, use AI for theme-spotting.\n7. **Present Findings** — Three output formats: Deal Reports (per-deal), Executive Summaries (quarterly), Sales Presentations (actionable battlecard intel).\n\n### Four Stages of Win-Loss Maturity (Ryan Sorley Framework)\n- **Stage 1: Sales-Sourced** — Sporadic CRM dropdown data, biased\n- **Stage 2: Siloed** — One department runs it, insights not shared\n- **Stage 3: Integrated** — Dedicated owner, cross-functional data, but lacking action\n- **Stage 4: Action-Oriented** — Dedicated owner, leadership support, systematic data, measurable actions taken\n\n### Interview Guide: 10 Buyer Journey Categories with 31 Questions\n1. **The Role** — \"How did you play a role in the evaluation process?\"\n2. **Awareness** — \"What made you realize you needed a vendor partner in this space?\"\n3. **Evaluation Bias** — \"What did you think of our company before the evaluation started?\"\n4. **Requirements** — \"How did you go about requirements gathering?\"\n5. **Consideration** — \"Who else did you evaluate? Explain factors that narrowed your decision.\"\n6. **Buying Committee** — \"Who were the most influential people in the decision-making process?\"\n7. **Product Demo** — \"What was the most memorable part of the demo experience?\"\n8. **Products & Services** — \"How would you describe our product strengths and weaknesses?\"\n9. **Price** — \"How did our pricing model compare to competitors?\"\n10. **Sales Process** — \"What was missing from the sales process and what did you like?\"\n\n### Klue 2025 Statistics (Survey of 313 Business Leaders)\n- **94%** of orgs maintaining or increasing win-loss budget\n- **98%** of programs have executive visibility\n- **56%** of VP/C-level say win-loss has helped increase win rates\n- **53%** of execs report more effective sales cycles\n- **70%** of execs use insights for GTM messaging/positioning\n- **67%** of win-loss programs managed alongside competitive intelligence\n- **Teams with integrated CI + win-loss are 2x more likely to report \"transformational impact\"**\n- Product Marketing owns win-loss at **41%** of orgs; Sales at 29%\n- **40%** of deals analyzed on average through win-loss\n- **70%** analyze deals within one month of close\n- **21%** of win-loss work is now AI-augmented\n\n### Key Data Point\nPer Anova Consulting research cited by Klue: **60% of sellers are partially or completely wrong about why they lost a deal.**\n\n---\n\n## 2. CLOZD — Dedicated Win-Loss Analysis Firm\n\n**Source URLs:**\n- https://www.clozd.com/blog/a-framework-for-creating-the-right-win-loss-analysis-questions\n- https://www.clozd.com/blog/kicking-off-your-first-win-loss-analysis-project\n- https://www.clozd.com/blog/four-pillars-of-effective-win-loss-analysis\n- https://www.clozd.com/blog/win-loss-analysis-for-product-marketers\n- https://www.clozd.com/blog/estimating-the-roi-of-your-investment-in-win-loss-analysis\n- https://www.clozd.com/solutions/win-loss-analysis\n\n### Methodology: 6-Step Program + 4 Pillars\n\n**6 Steps to Start:**\n1. Identify a revenue problem to investigate\n2. Develop an interview template\n3. Reach out to buyers\n4. Interview and survey buyers\n5. Analyze data for \"Decision Drivers\"\n6. Report findings to enact change\n\n**4 Pillars of Effective Win-Loss:**\n1. **Leadership & Culture** — Executive sponsorship required\n2. **Data Collection & Quality** — Semi-structured interviews, third-party interviewers reduce bias\n3. **Data Synthesis & Analysis** — Code and quantify findings\n4. **Adoption & Action** — Insights must drive change across the org\n\n### Interview Question Framework (5 Principles)\n1. **Start broad, open-ended** — \"What prompted you to evaluate solutions at this time?\" \"How did you structure your evaluation?\"\n2. **Determine core topics** — Product/Solution, Sales Experience, Pricing, Competitive Landscape, Implementation\n3. **Ask about specific competitors** — \"What were your impressions of [competitor]? Strengths? Weaknesses?\"\n4. **Use open-ended why/what questions** — Avoid quantitative scale-based questions during interview; save those for post-interview survey\n5. **Always ask 'what would have changed the outcome'** — The most actionable question\n\n### Product Marketer Operational Checklist (First 30 Days)\n- **Week 1:** Pick cohorts, draft invite + incentive, finalize script, set up tagging schema\n- **Week 2-3:** Run 15-25 interviews per segment, code quotes, produce first evidence pack (5-7 insights with buyer quotes + recommended actions)\n- **Week 4:** Publish \"Voice of the Buyer\" brief, implement 2-3 low-lift changes, set up monthly review cadence\n\n### Clozd's Deal Selection Criteria\n- Target 30-60 won and lost deals from last 2-8 weeks\n- Stratify by segment/ACV\n- Recruit buyers within 2-6 weeks of decision\n- Offer modest honorarium\n- Third-party interviewers recommended to reduce social desirability bias\n- 30-minute semi-structured interviews\n\n### ROI Data (from Clozd)\n- **10% improvement in win rates** is common in first year of implementing a win-loss program\n- For a company with $10M revenue and 20% win rate, a 10% improvement (to 22%) = **$1M incremental revenue**\n- **Gartner found certain companies observed up to 50% improvement in win rates**\n- Additional ROI: 10% decrease in sales ramp time for new hires\n\n---\n\n## 3. ANOVA CONSULTING GROUP — The Win-Loss Pioneers (20+ Years)\n\n**Source URLs:**\n- https://www.theanovagroup.com/2025/02/competitive-intelligence-win-loss-sales/\n- https://www.theanovagroup.com/2025/04/the-anatomy-of-an-effective-win-loss-program/\n- https://www.theanovagroup.com/2025/05/the-anatomy-of-an-effective-win-loss-program-part-three/\n- https://www.theanovagroup.com/win-loss-analysis-insights/in-the-news/implement/\n- https://www.theanovagroup.com/2021/04/win-loss-interview-guide/\n- http://theanovagroup.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/Anova_How_to_Implement_a_WinLoss_Program.pdf\n\n### Methodology: 7-Step Implementation\n\n1. **Identify a Program Coordinator** — Sales or marketing person with authority to drive cross-functional collaboration\n2. **Kickoff Meeting** — Head of sales MUST attend; all stakeholders share objectives, agree on workflow and timeline\n3. **Create & Finalize Interview Guide** — Cover all stages of sales cycle: vendor selection process, important attributes, decision criteria, strengths/weaknesses\n4. **Identify & Train Interviewers** — NOT the sales team; should be comfortable leading probing conversations; third-party preferred\n5. **Pilot the Program** — Start small, work out bugs\n6. **Conduct & Disseminate Interviews** — Central repository for transcripts, regular reporting cadence\n7. **Iterate & Improve** — Continuous improvement based on feedback\n\n### Interview Guide: 4 Key Components\n1. **Search Criteria** — \"What business problems were you trying to solve?\" Transport respondent back to beginning of their search\n2. **Sales Process** — Did the prospect feel your team was responsive, knowledgeable, professional?\n3. **Quantitative Ratings** — Ask prospect to rate attributes (collect benchmarkable data)\n4. **Decision Drivers** — \"What were the top reasons for your choice?\" Cross-reference with stated search criteria\n\n### Key Anova Research Findings\n- **60% of the time** a salesperson does NOT get the full and accurate truth about why they won or lost\n- Salespeople only hear the truth about **40%** of lost deals in new business situations\n- **Response rates with third-party interviewers: 50-60%** (vs. much lower for internal teams)\n- Live qualitative interviews remain the **gold standard** for generating actionable data\n- Context + benchmarking matters: \"If 42% of losses cite lack of value, is that better or worse than comparable firms?\"\n\n### Internal vs. Third-Party Decision Framework\n\n| Factor | Internal | Third-Party |\n|--------|----------|-------------|\n| Product Expertise | High | Moderate (trainable) |\n| Interviewing Expertise | Low-Moderate | High (specialized) |\n| Bandwidth | Limited | Dedicated |\n| Objectivity | Low (bias risk) | High (neutral) |\n| Cost | Lower upfront | Higher but more actionable |\n| Response Rates | Lower | 50-60% |\n\n### Anova's Position on AI\n- \"An advanced AI model is useless if its data source is faulty\"\n- Automation good for operational efficiency, but live qualitative interviews with conversational flow and clarifying probes remain the gold standard\n- AI best used for: transcription, sentiment parsing, pattern detection\n- NOT a replacement for skilled human interviewers on high-value accounts\n\n---\n\n## 4. PRIMARY INTELLIGENCE / TRUVOICE (Now Part of Corporate Visions)\n\n**Source URLs:**\n- https://www.primary-intel.com/win-loss-analysis-overview/\n- https://www.primary-intel.com/using-win-loss-analysis-marketing/\n- https://corporatevisions.com/blog/win-loss-analysis-competitive-intelligence/\n- https://corporatevisions.com/blog/the-business-case-for-win-loss-analysis/\n\n### Methodology: TruVoice Buyer Insights Platform\n\n- Combines survey instruments with interview services\n- Analyzes feedback across **5 critical decision drivers**: Product, Price, Company, Sales Experience, Customer Experience\n- Tracks trends over time by competitor, segment, deal size\n- Connects buyer feedback to seller skills and coaching\n\n### Key Research Findings (From Analysis of 6,000+ B2B Deals)\n- **Sellers who receive buyer feedback achieve up to 40% better win rates** vs. those who don't\n- Sellers who get feedback from **at least 3 deals** can significantly improve win rates\n- **50-70% disconnect** between sellers' perceptions and buyers' actual decisions\n- Companies see revenue increases of **15-30%** with detailed win-loss reporting\n- Up to **50% improvement in win rates** documented\n\n### Three Layers of Competitive Intelligence from Win-Loss\n1. **Visible Layer** — Features, pricing, public positioning (what competitors want you to see)\n2. **Shadow Layer** — Actual sales tactics, positioning moves, hidden vulnerabilities\n3. **Deep Layer** — Strategic intent, market expansion plans, partnership signals\n\n### Integration with Competitive Intelligence\n- Partnership with Crayon to embed win-loss insights directly into battlecards, newsletters, dashboards\n- First-ever technical integration combining win-loss data with CI deliverables\n\n---\n\n## 5. CRAYON — Competitive Intelligence Platform + Win-Loss Integration\n\n**Source URLs:**\n- https://www.crayon.co/\n- https://www.crayon.co/news/20230123/primary-intelligence-integration\n- https://www.crayon.co/blog/primary-intelligence-develops-a-market-first-integration-with-crayon\n\n### Win-Loss Integration Approach\n- Crayon does NOT conduct win-loss interviews themselves\n- Integrates with win-loss providers (Clozd, Primary Intelligence/TruVoice)\n- Embeds buyer insights from win-loss directly into CI deliverables: battlecards, newsletters, dashboards\n- Tracks and analyzes sales outcomes in competitive deals\n- 1:1 Coaching: Managers monitor rep performance against competition over time\n- Prioritizes competitors with data on which give sales team the most trouble\n\n### Crayon's MCP Server\n- Recently launched first Competitive Intelligence MCP server\n- Pushes battlecards, win/loss stories, competitor profiles, objection handling into AI workflows\n\n---\n\n## 6. McKINSEY & COMPANY — B2B Sales Effectiveness\n\n**Source URLs:**\n- https://www.mckinsey.com/capabilities/growth-marketing-and-sales/our-insights/growth-amid-uncertainty-jump-starting-b2b-sales-performance\n- https://www.mckinsey.com/capabilities/growth-marketing-and-sales/our-insights/five-ways-b2b-sales-leaders-can-win-with-tech-and-ai\n- https://www.mckinsey.com/capabilities/growth-marketing-and-sales/our-insights/five-fundamental-truths-how-b2b-winners-keep-growing\n\nMcKinsey does not publish a specific \"win-loss analysis\" methodology. However, their B2B sales research provides the strategic context in which win-loss operates:\n\n### McKinsey's 5 Acceleration Levers for B2B Growth\n1. **Stop the bleeding** — Reduce churn, win back customers (predictive modeling on customer intrinsics)\n2. **Win more at home** — Cross-sell, up-sell to increase share of wallet\n3. **Scale lead acquisition** — Gen AI for prospecting\n4. **Focus for impact** — Big-deal support teams to win where it counts\n5. **Optimize pricing** — 1% price increase = 6-14% operating profit uplift\n\n### Key McKinsey Data Points\n- B2B buyers now consult **10 digital sources** before making a purchase decision\n- B2B purchase decisions involve **5-16 stakeholders** spanning up to 4 departments\n- **74%** of B2B buyer teams experience difficulty reaching consensus\n- High-growth companies invest in sales operations at **1.4x the rate** of low-growth companies\n- **70%** of B2B buyers will prefer digital/rep-free buying experiences\n- B2B customers use an average of **10 interaction channels** (up from 5 in 2016)\n- AI-powered CRMs increase lead conversion rates by **30-50%** with predictive scoring\n- Revenue teams using automation report **27% higher win rates**\n\n### McKinsey's Competitive Intelligence via Gen AI\n- One MCO (managed care organization) used gen AI to process unstructured data from historical responses + publicly available contract records\n- Generated competitive intelligence in seconds\n- Cut time to assess competitors' capabilities by significant margin\n- This is essentially automated win-loss at the proposal level\n\n---\n\n## 7. BAIN & COMPANY — NPS + Customer Loyalty\n\n**Source URLs:**\n- https://www.bain.com/insights/do-your-b2b-customers-promote-your-business/\n- https://www.bain.com/consulting-services/customer-strategy-and-marketing/net-promoter-score-system/\n- https://www.bain.com/contentassets/024349fc94204c66abd4b1d0fffe159c/bain_brief_do_your_b2b_customers_promote_your_business.pdf\n\nBain does not publish a dedicated win-loss methodology. Their contribution is through NPS (which they created) and its correlation with retention and growth:\n\n### Bain NPS + Win Rate / Retention Correlation\n- **B2B loyalty leaders grow 4-8 percentage points above market annual growth rate**\n- Customers who are \"Promoters\" (NPS 9-10) have **3-12x the lifetime value** of \"Detractors\" (NPS 0-6)\n- **68%** of B2B executives say customers are less loyal than they used to be\n- NPS explains roughly **20-60% of variation in organic growth rates** among competitors\n- Industry Net Promoter leaders outgrow competitors by **>2x**\n- B2B brands see **8.5% increase in retention** if they close the loop with all customers\n- Quarterly NPS surveys yield **51% increase in retention** vs. 44% for annual surveys\n- Acquiring a new customer costs **5-25x more** than retaining an existing one (Bain/Invesp)\n\n### Bain's B2B NPS Design Principles\n- Tailor to industry dynamics\n- B2B involves multiple constituencies: gatekeepers, business leaders, operational users\n- Design around when, how, and with whom to engage\n- Consider channel structure, decision-making structure, and moments of truth\n- Aim for **60% response rate** in B2B NPS surveys\n- Survey multiple contacts in an account: **68% median retention** vs. 50% for single stakeholder\n\n---\n\n## 8. USER INTUITION — AI-Moderated Win-Loss (Emerging Leader)\n\n**Source URLs:**\n- https://www.userintuition.ai/posts/win-loss-analysis-complete-guide/\n- https://www.userintuition.ai/posts/ai-moderated-win-loss-analysis/\n- https://www.userintuition.ai/reference-guides/win-loss-analysis-best-practices-b2b/\n\n### Breakthrough Research: The 44-Point Price Gap\nFrom analysis of **10,247 post-decision buyer conversations** (Jan 2024 - Dec 2025):\n\n| Stated Loss Reason | Initially Cited | Actual Primary Driver | Gap |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| Price / Budget | 62.3% | 18.1% | **-44.2 pp** |\n| Implementation Risk | 4.1% | 23.8% | +19.7 pp |\n| Champion Confidence Failure | 2.7% | 21.3% | +18.6 pp |\n| Time-to-Value Anxiety | 7.2% | 16.9% | +9.7 pp |\n\n**Stated reason matched actual decision driver only 36% of the time.**\n\n### Laddering Methodology (5-7 Levels of Probing)\nOriginated in clinical psychology, adapted for win-loss:\n- Level 1: Surface answer (\"Your pricing was too high\")\n- Level 2: Context probe (\"Walk me through that evaluation\")\n- Level 3: Comparison probe (\"How did you weigh price vs. other factors?\")\n- Level 4: Decision probe (\"What would have changed the outcome?\")\n- Level 5-7: Root cause (\"If we had matched pricing, would you have chosen us?\")\n\n### Recommended Win/Loss Interview Ratio\n- **40% win interviews, 60% loss interviews**\n- Overweight losses because failure modes tend to be more diverse\n- Win interviews reveal what tipped decisions, how to replicate success\n\n### Program Metrics Framework\n**Operational Metrics:**\n- 60%+ buyer response rate (vs. industry-typical 15-20%)\n- Insights delivered within 72 hours of deal close\n- 100-300 interviews quarterly (vs. typical 15-25)\n\n**Business Impact Metrics:**\n- 5 percentage point win rate improvement within 6 months\n- Loss pattern reduction in targeted segments\n- Sales cycle duration changes\n\n### Cost Comparison\n| Approach | Cost | Turnaround |\n|---|---|---|\n| Traditional consultant-led | $15,000-$27,000 per study | 4-8 weeks |\n| AI-moderated platforms | $200 for 20 interviews ($10-20/interview) | 48 hours |\n| DIY (CRM fields, internal surveys) | $0 incremental | Ongoing but unreliable |\n\n---\n\n## 11. EVALUESERVE — CI Integration Framework\n\n**Source URL:**\n- https://www.evalueserve.com/blog/integrating-win-loss-analysis-into-your-competitive-intelligence-program/\n\n### Variables for Win-Loss Analysis Integration\n- Company size, Brand identity, Typical Client Persona, Lead Source\n- Deal type, Industry specifics, Sales methodology used\n- Integration with broader CI program for maximum strategic value\n\n---\n\n## 12. SIMON-KUCHER — Pricing + Win-Loss\n\n**Source URL:**\n- https://www.simon-kucher.com/en/insights/harnessing-win-loss-analysis-strategic-business-growth\n\n### Pricing-Specific Win-Loss Insights\n- Pricing strategies significantly impact win-loss ratios\n- Recommend segmented and dynamic pricing strategies informed by win-loss data\n- Win-loss analysis reveals how pricing influences customer decisions and competitive positioning\n- Customer data insights: price sensitivity, differentiation strategies\n\n---\n\n## CONSOLIDATED: LOSS REASON CODING TAXONOMY\n\nBased on all sources, the standard coding categories used across the industry:\n\n### Primary Categories\n1. **Product/Solution** — Feature gaps, capabilities, ease of use, integration, scalability, roadmap\n2. **Price/Value** — Pricing model, total cost of ownership, perceived value, packaging\n3. **Sales Experience** — Rep responsiveness, expertise, relationship, demo quality, follow-up\n4. **Company/Brand** — Reputation, stability, market presence, references, case studies\n5. **Implementation** — Deployment timeline, complexity, risk, professional services\n6. **Customer Support** — Post-sale support perception, SLAs, training\n7. **Competition** — Specific competitor advantage, switching costs, incumbent bias\n8. **Buying Process** — Internal politics, budget cycle, champion departure, no-decision\n\n### Advanced Sub-Categories (from User Intuition's ontology)\n- Implementation risk\n- Champion confidence failure\n- Time-to-value anxiety\n- Narrative simplicity (ability to explain internally)\n- Vertical credibility (industry-specific proof points)\n\n---\n\n## CONSOLIDATED: BEST PRACTICES FOR HEALTHCARE / ENTERPRISE SOFTWARE\n\nFrom across all sources:\n\n1. **Multi-stakeholder interviews are critical** — Healthcare buying committees include clinical users, IT, procurement, C-suite, and compliance. Interview multiple roles per deal.\n2. **Compliance and security are hidden decision drivers** — Often not stated initially but surface through laddering. HIPAA, data residency, audit trails.\n3. **Implementation risk is disproportionately important** — In enterprise healthcare, implementation risk ranks as the #1 actual loss driver (23.8%) despite being cited only 4.1% of the time initially.\n4. **Long sales cycles require timely feedback** — Healthcare deals can span 9-18 months. Interview at decision point, not contract signature.\n5. **Reference selling dominates** — \"Vertical credibility\" (specific case studies in same healthcare sub-vertical with ROI numbers) is a top actual decision driver.\n6. **Third-party interviewers essential** — Healthcare buyers especially reluctant to give honest feedback to vendor sales teams due to ongoing relationship dynamics.\n7. **Track by buyer persona** — Segment findings by clinical vs. IT vs. procurement vs. executive stakeholders.\n8. **Integration with existing systems is often the real blocker** — EHR integration, HL7/FHIR compliance, and existing vendor ecosystem lock-in frequently surface as true loss reasons.\n\n---\n\n## CONSOLIDATED: ROI DATA\n\n| Source | Metric | Data Point |\n|--------|--------|------------|\n| Clozd | Win rate improvement (first year) | 10% improvement typical |\n| Gartner (via Clozd) | Win rate improvement (best case) | Up to 50% |\n| Corporate Visions/Primary Intel | Win rate improvement with buyer feedback | Up to 40% better |\n| Challenger Inc. | Revenue increase from detailed W/L | 15-30% |\n| CSO Insights | Teams using W/L regularly | Higher win rates than those who don't |\n| Deloitte | Revenue growth from systematic feedback | 10-15% higher than competitors |\n| Bain | B2B loyalty leaders vs. market | 4-8 pp above market growth |\n| Bain | Promoter lifetime value vs. detractor | 3-12x higher |\n| McKinsey | 1% price increase impact | 6-14% operating profit uplift |\n| User Intuition | 5pp win rate improvement | $750K quarterly on $150K ACV deals |\n| Klue survey | Budget trend | 94% maintaining or increasing |\n\n---\n\nThis research covers all 10 requested sources (Klue, Clozd, Anova, Primary Intelligence/Corporate Visions, Crayon, McKinsey, BCG/Bain, Deloitte, Accenture) plus bonus sources (User Intuition, Evalueserve, Simon-Kucher, Challenger Inc.). The MBB firms (McKinsey, BCG, Bain) do not publish dedicated win-loss methodologies -- their contributions are through adjacent research on B2B sales effectiveness, NPS/loyalty, and competitive intelligence.
